Johan Christian Dahl (also known as John Christopher Dahl, Danish: [dɑːl]; 12 November 1788 – 14 October 1857) was a Norwegian artist. He is considered the first great romantic painter in Norway, the founder of the "golden age" of Norwegian painting. He was also the first acquire genuine fame and cultural renown abroad. Dahl is often described as "the father of Norwegian landscape painting" and is regarded as one of the great European Romantic painters. His work has influenced various generations of later Norwegian artists.

Dahl studied in Copenhagen under the Flemish history painter, Christian August Lorentzen, and in 1818 he went to Dresden to study with the German landscape painter, Caspar David Friedrich. He was inspired by the art of the Norwegian "golden age" of the 17th century as well as the Dutch Golden Age and the German Romanticism. His early works are often dark and gloomy, but after 1820 he began to paint more brightly coloured landscapes. He is best known for his paintings of Norwegian fjords and mountains, and he often depicted wild storms and dramatic light

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%GROUND_TRUTH%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
Johan Christian Claussen Dahl (February 24, 1788 – October 14, 1857), often known as J.C. Dahl, was a Norwegian artist who is considered the first great Romantic painter in Norway, the founder of the "Golden Age" of Norwegian painting, and one of the greatest European artists of all time. He is often described as "the father of Norwegian landscape painting" and is regarded as the first Norwegian painter ever to reach a level of artistic accomplishment comparable to that attained by the greatest European artists of his day. He was also the first to acquire genuine fame and cultural renown abroad. As one critic has put it, "J.C. Dahl occupies a central position in Norwegian artistic life of the first half of the 19th century."

Although Dahl spent much of his life outside of Norway, his love for his country is clear in the motifs he chose for his paintings and in his extraordinary efforts on behalf of Norwegian culture generally. Indeed, if one sets aside his own monumental artistic creations, his other activities on behalf of art, history, and culture would still have guaranteed him a place at the very heart of the artistic and cultural history of Norway. He was, for example, a key figure in the founding of the Norwegian National Gallery and of several other major art institutions in Norway, as well as in the preservation of Norwegian stave churches and the restoration of the Nidaros Cathedral in Trondheim and Håkonshallen in Bergen.
